  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_24f52c68-5e2c-4242-933a-f6d2a5fe3122'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText12648176217886302739" style="display:none">The war of Troy is looming, and all the kings of the Great Green are gathering, friends and enemies, each with their own dark plans of conquest and plunder.<br /><br />Into this maelstrom of treachery and deceit come three travellers; Piria, a runaway priestess nursing a terrible secret, Kalliades, a warrior with a legendary sword, and Banokles who will carve his own legend in the battles to come.<br /><br /><i>Shield of Thunder</i> takes the reader back into the glories and tragedies of Bronze Age Greece, reuniting the characters from <i>Lord of the Silver Bow; </i>the dread Helikaon and his great love, the fiery Andromache, the mighty Hektor and the fabled storyteller, Odysseus.</span>

<div id="review_122368186" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122368186" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122368186?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=supermen">supermen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=retellings-reimaginings-and-mashes">retellings-reimaginings-and-mashes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=military-fiction">military-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=good-guys">good-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=war-sff">war-sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122368186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13159827777826111926"><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&current=farsnworth-1-1-1.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339641i/696350.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>As you can see above, the math for this one is quite simple. This is book two of one of the best Heroic Fantasy series I have ever read. This sequel to the wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_' title='Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lord of the Silver Bow</a> is the middle installment of David Gemmell's Troy trilogy in which he superbly re-imagines the events leading up to and including the Trojan War. It is brilliant, original and terrifically entertaining. <br/><br/>Beginning several years after the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_' title='Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lord of the Silver Bow</a>, this book continues the build up to </span>
  <span id="freeText13159827777826111926" style="display:none"><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=farsnworth-1-1-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339641i/696350.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As you can see above, the math for this one is quite simple. This is book two of one of the best Heroic Fantasy series I have ever read. This sequel to the wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_" title="Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Silver Bow</a> is the middle installment of David Gemmell's Troy trilogy in which he superbly re-imagines the events leading up to and including the Trojan War. It is brilliant, original and terrifically entertaining. <br><br>Beginning several years after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_" title="Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Silver Bow</a>, this book continues the build up to the final battle for the City of Troy. Many of the best characters from the first book are around including Helikaon (aka Aeneas), Odysseus, Gershom (aka...that would spoil the surprise but when you learn you will have bricks dropping from your bowels), Andromache and Hektor. In addition, there are a whole host of new kick-ass participants. We have Peria, a fugitive priestess with a dark secret (oh how we love the dark secret). Plus we have new favorites Kalliades and Banokles, two larger than life <s>heroes</s> <s>villains</s> warriors in the grand Gemmell style. Finally, Achilles finally joins the cast in a BIG BIG way. <br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&amp;current=brad_pitt_troy.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339641i/696351.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The breadth of the story gets broader and depth of the characters continues to deepen. The writing is blood pumping and the plot is pure octane of the highest caliber. This series is quickly becoming one of my favorite series of all time. Gemmell was a master of this kind of story and this is him at the absolute top of his game. If you like well written epics with H.E.R.O.I.C. characters and N.A.S.T.Y. villains, than this series will leave you happier than Peter Griffin on Red Bull.<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Cartoon%20TV/?action=view&amp;current=red-bull_o_GIFSoupcom.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380339641ra/696352.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>5.5 to 6.0 stars. HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13159827777826111926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2542716215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2542716215" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2542716215?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345477026" href="/book/show/1281010.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Greek mythology &amp; historical fiction fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2542716215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13496965330603541678"><b>Another great read but might’ve worked better if I’m not binge reading it.</b><br/><br/><i>Shield of Thunder</i> is the second book in the Troy trilogy by David Gemmell and in the case of this book, I think I’ll start my review with the parts I didn’t like. Binge reading this book immediately after the first book was quite an odd experience. Not only the book starts with the characters sailing to Troy again just like the first half of the first book, after all the time I've spent reading Helikaon and the other chara</span>
  <span id="freeText13496965330603541678" style="display:none"><b>Another great read but might’ve worked better if I’m not binge reading it.</b><br /><br /><i>Shield of Thunder</i> is the second book in the Troy trilogy by David Gemmell and in the case of this book, I think I’ll start my review with the parts I didn’t like. Binge reading this book immediately after the first book was quite an odd experience. Not only the book starts with the characters sailing to Troy again just like the first half of the first book, after all the time I've spent reading Helikaon and the other characters that I'm starting to get familiar with, the first of of the book—with the exception of Odysseus—had the narrative centered on two new main characters, Kalliades and Banokles. It took me quite a while to get used to Kalliades and Banokles and part one of the book honestly almost made me put the book to my DNF pile. I was honestly super bored with the first 120 pages and the sudden changes in the main characters reminded me a lot of <i>The Desert Spear</i> by Peter V. Brett. Plus, there was also a non-explained time skip in which pivotal events have occurred off-screen.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Nothing of real worth can ever be bought. Love, friendship, honour, valour, respect. All these things have to be earned.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Luckily though, because the storytelling structure was similar to <i>The Desert Spear</i>, once the book entered part two and the main character started appearing again, my experience became significantly better. This of course doesn’t mean that Kalliades and Banokles were thoroughly boring. It’s just that in my opinion the first section of the book should’ve been intertwined with Helikaon, Andromache, Hector, and Achilles storyline instead of forcing the readers to read only Odysseus, Kalliades, and Banokles POV for more than 100 pages. That said, part one of the book really did help in fleshing out Kalliades and Banokles characters for the later section of the novel. Gemmell really put a lot of emphasis on friendship and love in this installment and he was able to do that because of Kalliades and Banokles friendship. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“I may be stupid, as you say, to believe in honour and friendship and loyalty without price. But these are virtues to be cherished, for without them we are no more than beasts roaming the land.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />In the matter of prose, <i>Shield of Thunder</i> was once again extremely well-written just like the first book. As events have started to escalate, Gemmell also portrayed the horror and tragedy that can come from war with many talents. Take a look at this passage for example:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“There is a darkness in you. In all of us, probably. Beasts we keep chained. Ordinary men have to keep the chains strong, for if we let the beast loose then society will turn upon us with fiery vengeance. Kings though...well, who is there to turn upon them? So the chains are made of straw. It is the curse of kings, Helikaon, that they can become monsters. And they invariably do.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />There were some exceptional passage and scenes like the one above. Not to mention that Hector and Achilles also have a more important role in this installment; I loved Gemmell’s retelling of Hector. However, I do wish that some of the battles didn’t happen off-screen. Gemmell is a pretty damn good author in building momentum. The emotions and tensions before a battle is going to happen was so damn real and well-written but the executions of the action scene itself were mostly pretty short or happened off screen which disappointed me a bit.<br /><br />Overall, I did have a great time with <i>Shield of Thunder</i> despite a few issues. The set pieces have been placed and everything should be leading towards the tragic Trojan War in the next and final book of the trilogy. I will read the conclusion of the trilogy pretty soon.<br /><br /><b>You can buy the book with free shipping by clicking this <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780345477026/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">link!</a></u></b><br /><br /><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2018/11/17/shield-of-thunder-troy-2/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13496965330603541678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1860809320" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1860809320" />
    <a title="Anish Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli"><img alt="Anish Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579696384p2/20963257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1860809320?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anish Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anish Kohli" href="/user/show/20963257-anish-kohli">Anish Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1860809320" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3514698710286178919">Humph…<br/>Tell me, have you read a book that has seen you at a loss for words? An experience so rich, you couldn’t possibly explain?<br/>This is that.<br/><br/>I had heaped praise on the author for the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840560022?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lord of the Silver Bow</a> and quite honestly did not hope for anything better in this book. But it was delivered, and in style. <br/>The book has mostly the same characters with a few strong characters being introduced. All the characters compliment each other in ways most apt.<br/>Hector, a great warrior, unmatched in skill and</span>
  <span id="freeText3514698710286178919" style="display:none">Humph…<br />Tell me, have you read a book that has seen you at a loss for words? An experience so rich, you couldn’t possibly explain?<br />This is that.<br /><br />I had heaped praise on the author for the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1840560022?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Silver Bow</a> and quite honestly did not hope for anything better in this book. But it was delivered, and in style. <br />The book has mostly the same characters with a few strong characters being introduced. All the characters compliment each other in ways most apt.<br />Hector, a great warrior, unmatched in skill and power, hateful of everything the war brings. A level headed man with compassion to guide him.<br />Achilles, a might hero, only one to challenge the great Hecktor, driven by thoughts of Blood and Glory. Relentless and a brute.<br />Banokles, a carefree fighter, full of life, living in the present.<br />Kalliades, a fearful soldier, a strategist and a resigned soul. <br />Kalliope, a woman of will, driven by love and love alone.<br /><br />This book stands in stark contrast to what the 1st book was. It has no clear lead character. No great epic war sequence. No heroes rise or fall. No great love. No great enmity.<br /><br />Then what does it have?<br /><br />It has the thing that I cherish the most. <b>STORY-TELLING.</b><br />Imagination so vast, so vivid, it is not possible to say it isn’t real.<br />Words? No, gems. Polished gems. Writing so smooth, silk would feel coarse in comparison.<br />Characters so life like, they pull you in &amp; capture you.<br />Different stories, of men and women, trying to understand what they live for, stand for and would die for.<br />Stories of greed and lust for power. To be Supreme. To reign over all. Stories of all that it is to be Human.<br /><br />This is the story of how and why the Trojan War was fought. The answer to which is put forth very eloquently by the author:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>It is the curse of kings, that they can become monsters. And they invariably do.</b>
</i><br />This book takes your hand and leads you to the battlefield where the final battle of Troy will unfold. It tells you of all the reasons why it should have happened the way it did.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Kings do not reign long if they let other Kings piss on their shoes.</b>
</i><br />What happens when wisdom has run its course?<br /><br /><i>
  <b>There is a darkness in all of us. Beasts, we keep chained. Ordinary men have to keep the chains strong. Kings, though....</b>
</i><br />What happens when for want of petty reasons, pride and ego, bonds deeper than family were forfeit?<br /><br /><i>
  <b>You are all so sad. I’m not. All the people I love…are with me…</b>
</i><br />What happens when a troubled soul stares death in the eye? They accept death. They welcome it. In their final moments, alongside with a few loved ones, the world seems complete. Beautiful. Serene. It is their sweet release.<br /><br />Killing off characters in most gruesome ways is easy. But to grant a tattered soul it’s release and to have the reader understand this, that is ingenuity. To make the reader’s heart ache, for the death of a character, for love lost, is the mark of an author.<br /><br />I have fallen in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11586.David_Gemmell" title="David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">David Gemmell</a>. This book is right there at the top with anything else for me. It has seen me mad when I thought Helikaon has been killed. It saw me elated to know he was alive. It brought me sadness when Kalliades lost hope. It saw me fraught with despair when Kalliope died. It saw me proud when Banokles rose to the occasion.<br /><br />This book, is the reason why I read, why I have reverence for the written word.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>Word after word after word, is POWER</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Ever since I started reading, I have believed that books are magic in their own right. You get to touch greatness, feel the elation, know deepest despair, hold love close, see battles waged, lives lost and bonds forged. Books transport you to a world of their own choosing and for a while, just a while, you are lost to the reality of this world. You are free to roam the pastures and lands and hill and mountains and seas and oceans.<br /><br />Books like these, authors like David Gemmell are not just authors. They are magicians. They are Saviors. They save many a soul from themselves. Give them a place where they can lose themselves to be found again, to break themselves to be made strong again.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>The world would be a sadder place without stories.</b>
</i><br /><br />I was saved not so long ago by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8349.Christopher_Paolini" title="Christopher Paolini" rel="nofollow noopener">Christopher Paolini</a> and his magic. Then I was not quite capable to thank him. Neither am I now. But this book has reminded me of just how much a story can impact you. How many faces have these people lit up with a smile. How many people they have instilled with hope and will. How many hearts they have touched. How many minds have they kept sane.<br /><br />This trilogy will stay with me, a reminder of what true magic is.<br /><br />Take a bow, Mr Gemmell. May your soul rest in peace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3514698710286178919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1263652812" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263652812" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263652812?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345477019" href="/book/show/44012.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263652812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13809275350576796525">In what should be a happy time with the heir to Troy getting married, knives are being sharpened as enemies prepare for war. Hidden plots and plans unfold in the intrigue laden Shield of Thunder.<br/><br/>For a book series about a massive looming war it sure takes a long time to get to it. From the beginning of Lord of the Silver Bow all the readers and characters knew a war was coming between Troy and Mykene yet there was only build up to the impending battle in book one. Surely The Shield of Thunder wit</span>
  <span id="freeText13809275350576796525" style="display:none">In what should be a happy time with the heir to Troy getting married, knives are being sharpened as enemies prepare for war. Hidden plots and plans unfold in the intrigue laden Shield of Thunder.<br /><br />For a book series about a massive looming war it sure takes a long time to get to it. From the beginning of Lord of the Silver Bow all the readers and characters knew a war was coming between Troy and Mykene yet there was only build up to the impending battle in book one. Surely The Shield of Thunder with a cover picture of <i>The</i> Trojan Horse would focus on the war itself...nope. The first 330 or so pages were more build up to the war. This time period revolved around Hektor and Andromache's wedding yet we don't even see the wedding in all that time. After that point there is a big time skip and the war has finally begun. Now being a war whose point of view would you expect to see? Warriors of course. Well we get a little of that, but then large point of view sections from a 3 year old boy and 2 queens. It's all quite frustrating to say it nicely. If not for Odysseus and Bankoles then I don't know if I could have finished this book.<br /><br />The Shield of Thunder is the third book I've read by David Gemmell and I'm starting to notice some patterns such as instant inexplicable love interests, constantly shifting point of views, random point of views, and the seriousness of war. I'm quite appreciative of the seriousness of war, but I find I've grown tired of the love interests and the way he makes use of point of view characters.<br /><br />The characters themselves largely feel flat to me. I don't feel as though I'm in their head experiencing emotions with them as much as I feel I'm being told about them having emotions by a third party. There is quite the emotional disconnect that only felt to be bridged by Odysseus and Banokles. I enjoyed my time when the two of them were point of view characters because they felt and behaved like real people constantly unlike the remaining cast of characters.<br /><br />I have found the retelling interesting to some degree as Paris and Helen are barely even involved. Apparently Helen is a plain and dull woman rather than the woman so beautiful men died fighting in a war over her. I didn't mind the focus on Helikaon in the first book, but he's largely absent in this book due to a festering injury caused by an assassin. Hektor and Achilles are largely forgettable even though they are still fearsome warriors and leaders of men. I think one of the parts of the retelling I like least is Priam being a scumbag rather than a fairly good man and great king.<br /><br />All in all Shield of Thunder was a long plodding book that was mainly a disappointment. I'm not sure at this point if I'll finish the series.<br /><br />2.5 out of 5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13809275350576796525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_548161045" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548161045" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548161045?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345477019" href="/book/show/44012.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548161045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13882326352017671590"> Originally reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.com/2013/07/28/fails-to-deliver-on-book-is-great-ending/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths Reviews</a> <br/><br/>Book I of this series started off slow but really picked up speed as it reached its conclusion, so I started book two very excited to see where Gemmell was going with it. Unfortunately, <i>Shield of Thunder</i> really failed to deliver.<br/><br/>As soon as you begin this book, you will notice that Gemmell has skipped forward in time. No big deal really except for one important fact: a tragic event has occurred, which has left one of our main characters dead or dying. (</span>
  <span id="freeText13882326352017671590" style="display:none"> Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.com/2013/07/28/fails-to-deliver-on-book-is-great-ending/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths Reviews</a> <br /><br />Book I of this series started off slow but really picked up speed as it reached its conclusion, so I started book two very excited to see where Gemmell was going with it. Unfortunately, <i>Shield of Thunder</i> really failed to deliver.<br /><br />As soon as you begin this book, you will notice that Gemmell has skipped forward in time. No big deal really except for one important fact: a tragic event has occurred, which has left one of our main characters dead or dying. (I suppose the author might have done this to build suspense or tension, but it had the affect of annoying me more than anything else.) And so, with this former main character in limbo, the focus of <i>Shield of Thunder</i> shifts to a brand new character, Piria, and two, minor characters, Kalliades and Banokles, from book one. <br /><br />Immediately, our new stars take center stage, uniting in tragic fashion before their backstory is revealed. Unfortunately, from this intriguing beginning, the story takes a big nosedive as the three journeying by sea to Troy (IF this sounds like deja vu after reading Book I I understand completely.), and even Odysseus' presence or the hopeless love of one of the companions for the other can't make this sea trip any better than the one in <i>Lord of the Silver Bow</i>. Honestly, if not for the constant interludes with Andromache in Troy itself, the book would have floundered from the start, but once again the city of Priam comes to the rescue, as the politically charged wedding games of Hektor and Andromache liven things up with political machinations, emotional fights, and the dramatic return of an old character. <br /><br />By the end of the wedding games, <i>Shield of Thunder</i> was right back on pace, rushing forward not only toward the beginning of the Trojan War but also toward the emotionally charged completion of Piria, Banokles and Kalliades' quest. But, alas, Gemmell once again crushed my hopes for this novel. Let me explain.<br /><br />One, the epic quest of Piria had been the major plot line in the book from page one. Gemmell spends chapters explaining it, making it heart-rending, and setting up a climatic ending to it. Then, when Piria, Banokles and Kalliades are moments away from completing it, things just . . . fizzle out. I won't explain how, but Piria's story just ends. No other way to say it. Boom it is gone, and you sit there and ask yourself why Gemmell spent all this time building this up to just snuff it out like a candle flame. Big letdown.<br /><br />Second, Gemmell skips forward in time again. The first time it was between book one and two, so I can live with that even though I didn't like it. Here, however, there is no reason for the time skip. One minute, there is a looming war between Mycene and Troy, and the next it has been going on for years. We hear about all these huge battles that have taken place. Characters talk about Hektor's victories and Odysseus' strategic brilliance, but what we actually read about is Kalliades and Banokles' struggles. And, while I did like both characters, Kalliades spends more time waxing philosophical on his inability to love anyone rather than actually fighting. <br /><br />Third, Gemmell has this annoying habit of giving you a character, feeding you a backstory then never returning to him. The Egyptian, Gershom, is a prime example. Book one starts off with him getting lots of page time; we get a detailed backstory with some plot issues twisting around. Then in <i>Shield of Thunder</i> Gershom goes poof! and disappears. Oh, he makes some appearances, but nothing related to his backstory. And he isn't the only character treated this way by the author. It is beyond irritating.<br /><br />So while <i>Shield of Thunder</i> is an okay read, I can't say I really liked it. Honestly, Gemmell barely keeps his Trojan War epic afloat with this one. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13882326352017671590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2932936791" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51196399-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597783321p2/51196399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2932936791?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/51196399-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2932936791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1417404802161447483">No question that David Gemmel was a brilliant writer and his second book in his Troy series is a riveting read full of action, wonders, sense and sensuality. It brings the Bronze Age to life in a very plausible way, as the story of the young King of Dardania Helikaon and his frustrated love for the beautiful Andromache. But the bulk of the book follows the adventures of two renegade Mykene warriors, Banokles and Kalliades, who rescue the mysterious and troubled beauty Piria. While I found the mi</span>
  <span id="freeText1417404802161447483" style="display:none">No question that David Gemmel was a brilliant writer and his second book in his Troy series is a riveting read full of action, wonders, sense and sensuality. It brings the Bronze Age to life in a very plausible way, as the story of the young King of Dardania Helikaon and his frustrated love for the beautiful Andromache. But the bulk of the book follows the adventures of two renegade Mykene warriors, Banokles and Kalliades, who rescue the mysterious and troubled beauty Piria. While I found the minimization of Helen of Troy as a plain and mousy character lacking significance difficult to digest as this is the essence of the Iliad, and likewise the emasculation of Hektor, the added dimensions made up for these disappointment's. The character of Gershom who we find out will be a major player in another historic saga is quite astounding. The battle scenes are gory and the cruelty of some of the generals and kings of the time is quite disturbing. But the passions and exploration of inner are equally well delivered. All in all a great installment in this historic fantasy thriller.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4999484000908058511">Continuation of Troy 1 [ Lord of the Silver Bow ], this book started off as interesting as its predecessor. Odysseus was focussed upon in more detail and I loved reading about him and listening to his tales of wit and wisdom. The other prominent characters were Kalliodes, who falls in love with Kalliope a.k.a Piria, the former lover of Andromache, who was a prominent character of the first book, and who is about to marry Hektor, the Prince of Troy. Kalliope is rescued from pirates by Kalliodes a</span>
  <span id="freeText4999484000908058511" style="display:none">Continuation of Troy 1 [ Lord of the Silver Bow ], this book started off as interesting as its predecessor. Odysseus was focussed upon in more detail and I loved reading about him and listening to his tales of wit and wisdom. The other prominent characters were Kalliodes, who falls in love with Kalliope a.k.a Piria, the former lover of Andromache, who was a prominent character of the first book, and who is about to marry Hektor, the Prince of Troy. Kalliope is rescued from pirates by Kalliodes and Banocles, and these three in turn seek shelter with Odysseus in his ship, later reaching Troy, meeting up with the Trojan royals, and finally ending up with Odysseus's army in the great war of Troy. The latter quarter of the book focuses upon the so far neglected queen Helioptes, who is forever battling with her fears of the cruel Myreans, which unfortunately come true. <br />It was a good read, but the latter quarter somehow negated the initial charm and ease of flow of the book and the characters. The war starts, bloodshed occurs and things look grim. <br />Overall, an enjoyable book, recommended to Greek mythology fans.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920065603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2351962591544177572">4.5 stars<br/><br/><b>I love it when I really like the first book in a series, and then the second book is even better!</b> I will say it took a little while before some of the main characters from the first book reappeared in this one, but honestly I didn't mind it much because I genuinely liked the 'new' characters too (technically they were in the first book too, but very minor roles).<br/><br/>This series is full of interesting characters, betrayals, alliances, intrigue, friendships, redemption, and battles; it's awes</span>
  <span id="freeText2351962591544177572" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br /><b>I love it when I really like the first book in a series, and then the second book is even better!</b> I will say it took a little while before some of the main characters from the first book reappeared in this one, but honestly I didn't mind it much because I genuinely liked the 'new' characters too (technically they were in the first book too, but very minor roles).<br /><br />This series is full of interesting characters, betrayals, alliances, intrigue, friendships, redemption, and battles; it's awesome. My one and only complaint so far with this series is that there are some instances of insta-love. But since the romance is such a minor point to the plot, it doesn't bother me like it usually does in books that are entirely focused on the romance in the first place.<br /><br />Sadly, the author died while writing the third book in this trilogy but his wife completed it for him. I'm interested to see how well she manages to pull off his writing style. I'll definitely be reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2351962591544177572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1599880110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599880110" />
    <a title="Shima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20404643-shima"><img alt="Shima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468228684p2/20404643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1599880110?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shima" href="/user/show/20404643-shima">Shima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780552151122" href="/book/show/526070.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599880110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12509248018873430742">Gemmell always does well to avoid second book syndrome, of course still the second book is always a little ways behind the awesome introduction first book and epic ending last one. <br/>What Gemmell does is dependent on his great strength as a writer, his characters. <br/><br/><b>In the second book he immediately introduces new characters, making you care for them and interested in their stories. Then just as the rush from the new characters is starting to wear off, The reader receives some news from the old and </b></span>
  <span id="freeText12509248018873430742" style="display:none">Gemmell always does well to avoid second book syndrome, of course still the second book is always a little ways behind the awesome introduction first book and epic ending last one. <br />What Gemmell does is dependent on his great strength as a writer, his characters. <br /><br /><b>In the second book he immediately introduces new characters, making you care for them and interested in their stories. Then just as the rush from the new characters is starting to wear off, The reader receives some news from the old and much beloved characters of the first book, so you'll continue reading with new strength, Thirsty for news from your favorite characters.</b><br /> <br />I'm not gonna lie it's a method than can be annoying. The author is practically baiting you with these little snippets. "Just read about the new characters a little bit longer and soon you'll hear about Helikaon, or Andromache or..." But there is no doubt that it's also effective. By the time we actually do get to hear about old characters, we've grown to love the new ones as well. <br /><br /><b>This book continues with the aftermaths of the battle between Mykene and Troy. We get to watch the brewing tensions and secret conspiracies explode into full fledged wars, while old, dark secrets are revealed causing surprising shifts in sides and putting friends against each other. </b><br /><br /><b>Gemmell does war like no one else. He makes it seem like a living, growing organ. </b>You know in books how sometimes you look at the strategies and war fare and suddenly see some huge solution just sitting there? Or how it's so easy to keep track of everything and everyone and it's obvious right from the start who's on who's side and who is going to lead a last minute battle and who is going to break through a siege? <br />There is none of that with Gemmell, there is messy battles, there is luck, there is heavy choices to be made with terrible consequences. He makes characters you love, and who love each other face off in battle, and you get to watch the choices they make from each side. You can see small battles from different sides of the world make a bigger picture and you can feel the tide of war changing. It's something else. <br /><br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12509248018873430742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78262019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2980283077161812058"><br/> Read Fantasy Book Critic's article <a href='http://fantasybookcritic.blogspot.com/2009/08/trojan-war-reinterpretation-troy.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Trojan War - A Reinterpretation: "The Troy Trilogy" by David and Stella Gemmell </a><br/><br/> Mini-review of SHIELD OF THUNDER: In the second book “Shield of Thunder” the reasons for Andromache’s betrothal to Hektor are laid bare & they are not what the reader will expect. In this earlier 1/3rd of the book we are introduced to 2 minor characters from the end of the 1st book namely Kalliades & Banokles who after the events in the climax of “LOTSB” have been left bereft.</span>
  <span id="freeText2980283077161812058" style="display:none"><br /> Read Fantasy Book Critic's article <a href="http://fantasybookcritic.blogspot.com/2009/08/trojan-war-reinterpretation-troy.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Trojan War - A Reinterpretation: "The Troy Trilogy" by David and Stella Gemmell </a><br /><br /> Mini-review of SHIELD OF THUNDER: In the second book “Shield of Thunder” the reasons for Andromache’s betrothal to Hektor are laid bare &amp; they are not what the reader will expect. In this earlier 1/3rd of the book we are introduced to 2 minor characters from the end of the 1st book namely Kalliades &amp; Banokles who after the events in the climax of “LOTSB” have been left bereft. While traveling as pirates they come across a girl named Piria who wants to travel to Troy for reasons unknown. Their path converges with Odysseus in a strange way &amp; later lead on to Troy where the great games are on as a part of Hektor’s marriage to Andromache.<br /><br />We are also reintroduced to Helikaon who is now married but has been befallen by a great calamity thanks to a certain character from the previous book. We are also given a glimpse of Achilles &amp; David Gemmell has written a rather different first meet between Hektor &amp; Achilles &amp; whilst traditionalists might not be pleased, readers will enjoy the encounter. We also get to see Paris &amp; Helen albeit quite differently from what we expect, both being minor characters .<br /><br />Gershorm also has to face his past to save the life of his friend. The second book in a trilogy is often the hardest to write and least liked book in a trilogy, however SOT manages to heighten the stakes as set by LOTSB with the introduction of new POV characters &amp; gives us a rather excellent reason for why the Trojan War will be fought. Somehow David Gemmell manages to outshine his previous effort &amp; set the stage for the final book where we know what’s going to happen but yet the reader will be curious to see how it all pans out &amp; of course see the epic battle between Achilles &amp; Hektor as well.<br /></span>

<div id="review_74731425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74731425" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2846441-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537371209p2/2846441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74731425?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/2846441-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345477026" href="/book/show/1281010.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2846441-karla?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74731425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer347712377182912168">The first half of the book is better than the second, as Gemmell does a good job of writing Odysseus while sticking to his canonical attributes. The book takes a downturn, however, in the second half as Gemmell's stable of characters go from dire circumstances to mandatory last-minutes rescues to sudden deaths, all without much emotional involvement. So much of what makes these people tick is told, not shown, in pluperfect flashbacks, as was the case in the first book, and it was a worn-out devi</span>
  <span id="freeText347712377182912168" style="display:none">The first half of the book is better than the second, as Gemmell does a good job of writing Odysseus while sticking to his canonical attributes. The book takes a downturn, however, in the second half as Gemmell's stable of characters go from dire circumstances to mandatory last-minutes rescues to sudden deaths, all without much emotional involvement. So much of what makes these people tick is told, not shown, in pluperfect flashbacks, as was the case in the first book, and it was a worn-out device by this middle-child entry. The "hidden identity" ploy was used yet again and the true name of "Piria" was easily guessed within the first few pages. There were few surprises in this book.<br /><br />Considering how Gemmell has toyed with Homer's characters in their physical features, personalities, etc, I wish he had decided to rename them because some are either unrecognizable or ill-served by stupid cliches like the "war wound" and "healing sex." Maybe Gemmell fancied himself an iconoclast, like taking heroic Hector and turning him into a reluctant, anachronistic warrior beaten down by father &amp; country, but it's too much all in one place. Apart from Odysseus, I liked the references to regional politics and warring tribes and how Troy found itself squared against most of them. Unfortunately, Gemmell's inability to make the characters as interesting as their times brings it down.<br /><br />At any rate, while it was a fast read, it wasn't all that memorable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="347712377182912168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151859435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151859435" />
    <a title="Iset" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4973578-iset"><img alt="Iset" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563895104p2/4973578.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151859435?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iset" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iset" href="/user/show/4973578-iset">Iset</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4973578-iset?shelf=bronze-age-5000-to-1100bce-fiction">bronze-age-5000-to-1100bce-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151859435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer87861001054915695">There’s not too much I can add to my review of this, the second novel in the trilogy, without repeating what I said in my review of the first book. Gemmell’s writing quality is consistent throughout the series, and, like the first, this novel is packed with just as much adventure, tension, authentic detail and earthy characterisations. I liked the fact that Gemmell shifts gears here to three new lead characters – Kalliades, Banokles and Piria, who are barely more than mentioned in the first nove</span>
  <span id="freeText87861001054915695" style="display:none">There’s not too much I can add to my review of this, the second novel in the trilogy, without repeating what I said in my review of the first book. Gemmell’s writing quality is consistent throughout the series, and, like the first, this novel is packed with just as much adventure, tension, authentic detail and earthy characterisations. I liked the fact that Gemmell shifts gears here to three new lead characters – Kalliades, Banokles and Piria, who are barely more than mentioned in the first novel, and whose fates tie in with those of the previous book’s main characters. I mistakenly read this second instalment in the series first, and I don’t know if that had something to do with it, but I liked these leads even better than those in <i>Lord of the Silver Bow</i>. Argurios was fictional, but Andromache and Aeneas are well-known, if secondary, characters from the myth, and though Gemmell changes them around enough that you feel uncertain about their fate, with three fictional characters taking centre stage it really built up the anticipation for me, and the sense that literally anything could happen to these three characters that I had come to care about and I had no idea what lay in store for them. Just like the first book, I found this one to be a compelling page-turner, and the alterations to the legend that Gemmell makes in fact more historically accurate and a fresh new angle on the tale.<br /><br /><b>8 out of 10.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="87861001054915695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9953687041762447440"><b>Oh God!</b><br/><br/>What is it David Gemmell does to make such an epic story with amazing characters and breathtaking scenes!<br/><br/>This is the second book of the Troy trilogy and was outstanding just like the first one.   <span id="freeText9953687041762447440" style="display:none"><b>Oh God!</b><br /><br />What is it David Gemmell does to make such an epic story with amazing characters and breathtaking scenes!<br /><br />This is the second book of the Troy trilogy and was outstanding just like the first one. But, in my opinion, i have to say that i like far more the first book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_" title="Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Silver Bow</a> than this one. Shield of Thunder felt, in some parts, a bit slow in contrast with the first one where everything was fast paced and epic with every page you turn. I felt this book had so much of telling of the battles that were taking place and sometimes felt like it wasn't exciting enough that way, but immediately it contained other stories and plot happening that was making up for those parts, so it still, for me, deserves 5 stars.<br /><br />This book starts 1 year, i think, after the first book finished, and here you start seeing how everything evolves. How some battles started, how some characters became enemies of certain territories, how some kings started to ally with others and other important characters are introduced.<br /><br />The characters are well drawn, you really feel for them and their actions seem real.<br /><br />This is an amazing series! I'm so glad I found out about it and even happier that i already have the third book waiting for me!</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3393976395?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/76396700-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345477019" href="/book/show/44012.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393976395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14295601278494418210">The sophomore of the Troy trilogy does not falter as many do, but definitely takes a different approach to the story. Set roughly three years after the first, the Trojans and Agamemnon with his allies have been at war for three years. Most of this has thus far been at sea, although the noose is tightening on Troy. <br/><br/>This volume largely stays with a group of characters for a long time, and then shifts to other groups. We start with the only two Mykenes left from the thwarted raid on Troy from the f</span>
  <span id="freeText14295601278494418210" style="display:none">The sophomore of the Troy trilogy does not falter as many do, but definitely takes a different approach to the story. Set roughly three years after the first, the Trojans and Agamemnon with his allies have been at war for three years. Most of this has thus far been at sea, although the noose is tightening on Troy. <br /><br />This volume largely stays with a group of characters for a long time, and then shifts to other groups. We start with the only two Mykenes left from the thwarted raid on Troy from the first volume; the remaining solders returned to Mykene and were put to death except for the two that escaped. Kalliades and Banokles joined a pirate crew to escape, but deserted the crew to save the life of a young woman the pirates had captured that day. These three made their way and found Odysseus and joined his crew. The plot is too detailed and complicated to give a detailed account without spoilers.<br /><br />Like the previous volume in the series, Gemmell's complex plotting and narrative prose excel, while also pondering the human condition. Good stuff! While the battle scenes are few and far between, they are as usual excellently done. 4.5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14295601278494418210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17128959002190573559">This carries on directly from book 1. This isn’t a stand alone: you definitely have to read the first book first for this to make any sense, and it ends very much looking forward to the third book in the trilogy.<br/><br/>A huge plus for me is Gemmell’s re-imagining of Homeric myth. Iconic elements of the original are cleverly re-imagined in an almost throwaway style. His vibe is taking the Iliad as a garbled Chinese-whispers style hash-up of what ‘really happened’ - and his story is underpinned by contem</span>
  <span id="freeText17128959002190573559" style="display:none">This carries on directly from book 1. This isn’t a stand alone: you definitely have to read the first book first for this to make any sense, and it ends very much looking forward to the third book in the trilogy.<br /><br />A huge plus for me is Gemmell’s re-imagining of Homeric myth. Iconic elements of the original are cleverly re-imagined in an almost throwaway style. His vibe is taking the Iliad as a garbled Chinese-whispers style hash-up of what ‘really happened’ - and his story is underpinned by contemporary theories of the late bronze-age collapse.<br /><br />I enjoyed it a lot, although its structure is a little messy. The main plot line peters out about two-thirds of the way in, and the last third can be seen as a virtually discrete prologue to book 3, enlivened by Gemmell’s great writing of suspense and action scenes.</span>

  <span id="freeText12384649964486689552" style="display:none">Reading for the second time and can safely say while it's a great read, it's not going to be among my favorites...it lacks the Epic feel(Just cant compare to Illaid). Luckily had forgotten many of the best moments from the books so the surprise was maintained during the second read and had fun going over it again. <br /><br />It's a better book then the first one for many reasons. It's got more involvement of the ancient heroes. It finally brings out the Trojan War and in a realistic manner with battle raging all over the Aegean. <br /><br />But what i loved the most are the characters. Loved the way Odysseus was forced in the Mykene camp. How Andromache manipulates and handles Priam and Hekuba. Also the character of Banokles and his battles scenes in the ending is fun. The tragedy of Hektor is a awesome twist. These stuff make the book a great read.<br /><br />Would have like if there were more of Achilles and Kassandra two of my favorite characters from the Trojan War. Funny thing why the book is not Epic is there are too many small things happening. Too many minor characters. <br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText9487250503755646664" style="display:none">A lovely story. A fine re-imagining of the events leading up to the fall of Troy. I agree with the good reviews except calling it 'best book ever.' Second book of a trilogy. I did not read the first book but there are just enough references from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/257149.Lord_of_the_Silver_Bow__Troy___1_" title="Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy, #1) by David Gemmell" rel="nofollow noopener">Lord of the Silver Bow</a> to connect the dots between events. This installment can stand alone.<br /><br />Gemmell initially focuses on unintentional heroes Kalliades and Banokles. Their sub-story really helps tie these epic events together in an accessible way. It has all the makings of a great buddy picture. Reminds me of R2D2/C3PO, or perhaps Tahei and Matashichi of 'The Hidden Fortress,' or Looney Tunes' Benny and George. Like Forrest Gump, they are in the right places at the right times.<br /><br />The Gods play little to no role at all. <br /><br /></span>

But my enjoyment of this one was more around a 2 star. Giving it 3 because I'm probably just being ungenerous, but I was super relieved to get the end of this too-long tome. <br />Couple of mild spoilers ahead, but not hiding the review because they're mild. And if you're reading this and don't want mild spoilers, here's your warning.<br />The reinterpretation was fine. He did a good job of making sure that his change-ups (Helen as a pleasant plain girl, Hektor as impotent, Andromache as a badass lesbian) were internally consistent. The action is tempered with character insights. There's humor sprinkled throughout. <br />I especially enjoyed the pair of warriors who reminded me strongly of the protagonists in the 'Rome' mini-series.<br />But it never gripped me. I never dove into it. I never once climbed into bed with the delighted anticipation of picking it up. <br />It was one of the books I promised myself not to spend time on any more, and a long one at that.<br />Just not my cup of tea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10265387757156206826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1787456452195340183" style="display:none">I'm breezing past this series even though I really need to STOP. But I can't, because it's been a quite a while since I've been this addicted, and I really missed the thrill of it. I can't believe more people haven't read this series, mainly because Gemmell is such a good storyteller. That being said, this series is definitely not for everyone. There's a lot of graphic description of violence. There's murder, rape and all sorts of bad things done by brutal men and women. But what I'm really enjoying is the unpolished depiction of humanity, especially the nobility. The characters are multi-faceted and it is difficult to predict the course of actions they would take (it was for me, at least) which makes it so much more difficult to put the book down.</span>

<div id="review_68013586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68013586" />
    <a title="Nathan Trachta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2079440-nathan-trachta"><img alt="Nathan Trachta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400593090p2/2079440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68013586?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan Trachta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan Trachta" href="/user/show/2079440-nathan-trachta">Nathan Trachta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345477026" href="/book/show/1281010.Shield_of_Thunder">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68013586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer561485195725883227">A passion of mine is the story of the sacking of Troy and the return of the "Greeks" (The Iliad (Penguin Classics) and The Odyssey) while I'm no expert, I'm `acquainted' with the story. The events Homer describes are so strong and vivid, I also love the characters involved, particularly the character of Odysseus (sorry, rather than the big heroic type I'm more into the thinker).<br/><br/>Mr. Gemmel did the ambitious act of writing a series of historical fiction books that supported Homer's works along wit</span>
  <span id="freeText561485195725883227" style="display:none">A passion of mine is the story of the sacking of Troy and the return of the "Greeks" (The Iliad (Penguin Classics) and The Odyssey) while I'm no expert, I'm `acquainted' with the story. The events Homer describes are so strong and vivid, I also love the characters involved, particularly the character of Odysseus (sorry, rather than the big heroic type I'm more into the thinker).<br /><br />Mr. Gemmel did the ambitious act of writing a series of historical fiction books that supported Homer's works along with Virgil's The Aenid. The second in the series, Shield of Thunder picks up about three years after the first (Lord of the Silver Bow (Troy Trilogy, Book 1)), the setting is before the Iliad with growing tension between the Western Kings and those supporting Troy. Telling the tale this time, Mr. Gemmel decided on two parts, one focusing on the growing tension between the East and the West (The Gathering Storm, the focus is on Odysseus and the "changing" environment that leads to the Trojan War) and the engagements leading to the Iliad (An Enemy of Troy).<br /><br />Rating wise this is a solid 4 star book for me; and that's lower than I was initially anticipating. I say that because The Gathering Storm showed so much that made me love the book. Mr. Gemmel's description of Odysseus, Agamemnon, and the other greats from the Iliad was so interesting. I loved how Mr. Gemmel expanded Odysseus's story from Homer's and gave us so much to explain why he was the thinker and to be more feared by the Trojans than Agamemnon. Merging this with the story of Kalliades, Banokles, and Piria (sorry, you have to read it to learn about them) made for exquisite story telling (truly going to 5 stars). An Enemy of Troy though let things down. Part of the reason is the story grew in complexity due to the number of view points (we now see Helikaon, The Trojan Horse, and the Dardanian front) and Mr. Gemmel decided to lean more on fiction and less on history. I say that this is more fiction than history because Mr. Gemmel took the liberty of describing an environment more suited to the Dark Ages than that of the late Bronze, early Iron Ages : the cavalry is mounted rather than using chariots that history indicates (sorry, the mounted charges he describes wouldn't have been nearly as effective due to the lack of spurs and stirrup in that era) and the armor doesn't sound like the plate armor found in Mycenae grave sites, rather more like scale mail from later eras. I also had some problems with the "strategic" nature of the war. I say this because the war is being fought across a rather large area and uses strategy and logistical concerns that fit latter eras. While I admire Mr. Gemmel's idea on what was happening to Troy (attacking the supporting city states and then Troy, and yes, that's how I believe the 10 year `siege' of Troy occurred) I believe he made it a little to big and grand (sorry, the fighting we're reading about is largely on the Western side of the Dardanelles and I have a hard time believing Troy would have a significant land force there). Despite my issues though, Mr. Gemmel does deliver a nice story that seems to lend itself to Homer's and because of this it lends itself to a nice 4 star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="561485195725883227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
